The Necessity of Simultaneous Lifting of a Smooth Surface
Argument that lifting a smooth surface requires simultaneous elevation of all parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a smooth surface must be lifted all at once, based on the argument that partial lifting would cause the surface to disintegrate.

Core Idea
Lifting part of a surface tears it apart — so it must rise as one.

This passage presents a logical proof that if one smooth surface is raised from another, the entire upper surface must rise in a single instant. The argument relies on the impossibility of separation between connected parts, using the familiar analogy of a millstone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: a condition, a hypothetical, and a conclusion.
The key term 'رفع' (lifting) appears multiple times.
2
Identify the condition
The passage begins by stating that it is not impossible to raise one smooth surface from another all at once. This is the allowed scenario.
'دفعة' means 'at once' or 'simultaneously'.
3
Examine the hypothetical of partial lifting
The argument then considers what would happen if only some parts of the upper surface rose while others did not. This would lead to separation (انفكاك) between connected parts.
4
Understand the millstone analogy
The separation is compared to the disintegration of a millstone (تفكك الرحى): if one part moves and another does not, the object breaks.
This analogy is a standard kalam example for connected bodies.
5
Conclude the necessity of simultaneous lifting
Since such disintegration is impossible for a continuous smooth surface, all parts must rise together without any lag. The conclusion is that lifting must be 'all at once'.
The phrase 'بلا تخلف' means 'without lagging'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يمتنع رفع إحداهما عن الأخرى دفعة) بأن يرتفع جميع جوانبها معاً (لو ارتفع بعض إحداهما دون البعض لزم الانفكاك بين أجزاء الصفحة العليا فإنه إذا ارتفع بعض أجزائها عن السفلى، ولم يرتفع عنها الجزء المتصل بذلك المرتفع انفك أحدهما عن الآخر بالضرورة على قياس ما ذكروه في نفس الجزء من تفكك الرحى. وهكذا نقول في سائر الأجزاء فيجب ارتفاعها بأسرها معاً بلا تخلف. بل دفعة واحدة
And it is not impossible to raise one of them from the other at once, such that all its sides rise together. (If some part of one of them rose without the others, then separation among the parts of the upper surface would necessarily occur. For if some of its parts rose from the lower [surface] while the part connected to that raised part did not rise, then one would separate from the other necessarily, analogous to what they mentioned concerning the part itself of the disintegration of the millstone. And thus we say concerning the remaining parts, so it is necessary that all of them rise together without lagging. Rather, at once.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a proof that if one smooth surface is raised from another, the entire upper surface must rise simultaneously in a single instant. The argument is: if only some parts rise while others remain, then the connection between a rising part and a non-rising adjacent part would break, causing the surface to disintegrate. This is compared to the millstone argument: if a part of the millstone moves and another does not, the stone must break. Since such disintegration is impossible for a continuous surface, all parts must rise together at once.

Key Terms
رفع
انفكاك
الصفحة
دفعة
تفكك الرحى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A smooth surface can be lifted gradually, one part after another, without breaking.
Correction: The passage argues that gradual lifting would cause the parts to separate because adjacent parts would not move together, leading to disintegration. Hence, the entire surface must rise simultaneously.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if only some parts of the upper surface rise while others do not?
A) The surface remains intact.
B) The surface disintegrates.
C) A vacuum is created.
D) The lower surface rises as well.

Key Takeaway
A smooth surface cannot be lifted partially; it must rise all at once to avoid disintegration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you try to change only some parts of your character while leaving others unchanged? What 'tears' in your integrity as a result of that partial approach?
?
When you accept one truth from this lesson but resist applying it to other areas of your faith, do you sense the 'disintegration' that happens inside you? Will you commit today to embracing the whole truth about your accountability before Allah?
?
The surface cannot be lifted piece by piece without breaking. Is there a relationship, habit, or duty you are trying to 'lift' halfway — giving partial effort? What connection will break if you don't give it your full and simultaneous attention?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
From Indivisible Part to Vacuum
Proof that raising a surface at once creates vacuum using indivisible parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the impossibility of indivisible parts forces the conclusion that a vacuum must result when a surface rises all at once.

Core Idea
If a whole surface rises at once, vacuum must appear between it and the lower surface.

This passage presents a refined version of the second proof for the possibility of vacuum. It targets opponents who deny atoms and shows that even without assuming atoms, raising a surface at once forces a vacuum. The argument uses a conditional chain: if the rising part were indivisible (an atom), that would be impossible; therefore the whole surface must rise as one, leaving no body in between.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how the argument is structured as a conditional: 'if... then...'.
The parentheses in the Arabic indicate the original text of al-Mawaqif.
2
Follow the logical steps
Identify the key steps: a part of the upper surface rises at once; if that part were not a surface divisible in two directions, it would be an indivisible part (atom); but atoms are impossible according to the opponent; hence the part must be divisible, meaning the whole surface can rise at once.
The conclusion that vacuum follows is based on the absence of any other body between the two surfaces.
3
Reflect on the necessity of vacuum
Understand that the vacuum results necessarily because no body fills the gap; otherwise bodies would overlap (interpenetration), which is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً فأي جزء من أجزاء الصفحة العليا ( ارتفع ) عن السفلى (دفعة ) واحدة ( لو لم تكن صفحة ) منقسمة في جهتين ( كان ذلك ) الجزء المرتفع ( جزءاً لا يتجزأ ) أو ما في حكمه (وهو محال عندكم) فقد ثبت إمكان ارتفاعها عنها دفعة واحدة ) فإذا فرضنا ارتفاعها عنها) كذلك ( وقع الخلاء ) فيما بين الصفحتين (ضرورة) أنَّه لم يكن فيما بينهما جسم آخر وإلا لزم تداخل الأجسام
And also: whichever part of the parts of the upper surface rises from the lower [surface] at one instant, if it were not a surface divisible in two directions, then that raised part would be an indivisible part or what is in its ruling, and that is impossible according to you. So the possibility of the entire surface rising from it at once is established. Then if we suppose its rising from it in that manner, a vacuum would occur between the two surfaces necessarily, because there is no other body between them, otherwise overlapping of bodies would be necessary.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage provides a second proof for the possibility of a vacuum. It argues: suppose a part of the upper surface rises at once. If that part is not a surface (i.e., not divisible in two dimensions), then it would be an indivisible part (atom), which the opponent (philosopher) denies. Therefore, the part must be a divisible surface, meaning the entire surface can rise at once. When the whole surface rises, there is no body between the two surfaces, so a vacuum necessarily occurs. The alternative—that some other body fills the gap—is rejected because it would require the interpenetration of bodies.

Key Terms
جزء لا يتجزأ
صفحة
خلاء
تداخل الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Vacuum is impossible because air would rush in immediately.
Correction: The argument is purely about the absence of any body (including air) between the surfaces; it does not rely on whether the gap is filled later.

Checkpoint
Why does the possibility of the entire upper surface rising at once lead to a vacuum?
A) Because air cannot move into the gap.
B) Because there is no body between them and no other body moves in.
C) Because the lower surface also rises.
D) Because the parts disintegrate.

Key Takeaway
The vacuum necessarily results from the absence of any body between two surfaces when they separate at once, given the impossibility of indivisible parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a comfortable belief about the world (like 'nature abhors a vacuum') despite rational evidence to the contrary? What would it cost you to follow the argument wherever it leads?
?
This proof uses the very impossibility your opponents rely on to force a conclusion. Is there an area of your life where you are using your own weakness as an excuse to avoid a hard truth? What would it look like to use that weakness as a stepping stone instead?
?
The vacuum is real even though unseen and intangible. What invisible realities (like the afterlife, God's presence, or your own accountability) do you treat as unreal because you cannot sense them? What would change if you acted as if they were more real than what you see?
